class="mediawiki ltr sitedir-ltr mw-hide-empty-elt ns-0 ns-subject mw-editable page-Michelson&#8211;Morley_experiment rootpage-Michelson&#8211;Morley_experiment skin-vector action-view"> <div class="noprint" id="mw-page-base"></div>\n<div class="noprint" id="mw-head-base"></div>\n<div class="mw-body" id="content" role="main">\n<a id="top"></a>\n<div class="mw-body-content" id="siteNotice"><!-- CentralNotice --></div><div class="mw-indicators mw-body-content">\n</div>\n<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Michelson&#8211;Morley experiment</h1> <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">\n<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div> <div id="contentSub"></div>\n<div id="jump-to-nav"></div> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>\n<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>\n<div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Michelson_morley_experiment_1887.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="432" data-file-width="742" decoding="async" height="175" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Michelson_morley_experiment_1887.jpg/300px-Michelson_morley_experiment_1887.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Michelson_morley_experiment_1887.jpg/450px-Michelson_morley_experiment_1887.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Michelson_morley_experiment_1887.jpg/600px-Michelson_morley_experiment_1887.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Michelson_morley_experiment_1887.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Figure 1. Michelson and Morley\'s interferometric setup, mounted on a stone slab that floats in an annular trough of mercury.</div></div></div>\n<p>The <b>Michelson&#8211;Morley experiment</b> was an attempt to detect the existence of <a href="/wiki/Aether_theories" title="Aether theories">aether</a>, a medium permeating space that was thought to be the carrier of light waves. The experiment was performed between April and July 1887 by <a href="/wiki/Albert_A._Michelson" title="Albert A. Michelson">Albert A. Michelson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Edward_W._Morley" title="Edward W. Morley">Edward W. Morley</a> at what is now <a href="/wiki/Case_Western_Reserve_University" title="Case Western Reserve University">Case Western Reserve University</a> in <a href="/wiki/Cleveland" title="Cleveland">Cleveland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ohio" title="Ohio">Ohio</a>, and published in November of the same year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-michel2_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-michel2-1">[1]</a></sup> It compared the <a href="/wiki/Speed_of_light" title="Speed of light">speed of light</a> in perpendicular directions, in an attempt to detect the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Relative_motion" title="Relative motion">relative motion</a> of matter through the stationary <a href="/wiki/Luminiferous_aether" title="Luminiferous aether">luminiferous aether</a> ("aether wind"). The result was negative, in that Michelson and Morley found no significant difference between the speed of light in the direction of movement through the presumed aether, and the speed at right angles. This result is generally considered to be the first strong evidence against the then-prevalent <a href="/wiki/Aether_theories" title="Aether theories">aether theory</a>, and initiated a line of research that eventually led to <a href="/wiki/Special_relativity" title="Special relativity">special relativity</a>, which rules out a stationary aether.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-staley_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-staley-2">[A 1]</a></sup> Of this experiment, <a href="/wiki/Albert_Einstein" title="Albert Einstein">Einstein</a> wrote, "If the Michelson-Morley experiment had not brought us into serious embarrassment, no one would have regarded the relativity theory as a (halfway) redemption."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Folsing_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-Folsing-3">[A 2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>219</span></sup>\n</p><p>Michelson&#8211;Morley type experiments have been repeated many times with steadily increasing sensitivity. These include experiments from 1902 to 1905, and a series of experiments in the 1920s. More recent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Optical_resonator" title="Optical resonator">optical resonator</a> experiments confirmed the absence of any aether wind at the 10<sup>&#8722;17</sup> level.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Eisele_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-Eisele-4">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Herrmann2_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-Herrmann2-5">[3]</a></sup> Together with the <a href="/wiki/Ives%E2%80%93Stilwell_experiment" title="Ives&#8211;Stilwell experiment">Ives&#8211;Stilwell</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kennedy%E2%80%93Thorndike_experiment" title="Kennedy&#8211;Thorndike experiment">Kennedy&#8211;Thorndike experiments</a>, Michelson&#8211;Morley type experiments form one of the fundamental <a href="/wiki/Tests_of_special_relativity" title="Tests of special relativity">tests of special relativity</a> theory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rob_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-rob-6">[A 3]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="toc" id="toc"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" style="display:none" type="checkbox"/><div class="toctitle" dir="ltr" lang="en"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toclevel-2 tocsection-15"><a href="#Optical_tests"><span class="tocnumber">5.1</span> <span class="toctext">Optical tests</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-16"><a class="toctext">Notes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-21"><a href="#Experiments"><span class="tocnumber">7.2</span> <span class="toctext">Experiments</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-22"><a href=\'#Bibliography_(Series_"A"_references)\'><span class="tocnumber">7.3</span> <span class="toctext">Bibliography (Series "A" references)</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-23"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Detecting_the_aether">Detecting the aether</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Michelson%E2%80%93Morley_experiment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Detecting the aether">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Physics" title="Physics">Physics</a> theories of the late 19th century assumed that just as surface water waves must have a supporting substance, i.e. a "medium", to move across (in this case water), and audible <a href="/wiki/Sound" title="Sound">sound</a> requires a medium to transmit its wave motions (such as air or water), so light must also require a medium, the "<a href="/wiki/Luminiferous_aether" title="Luminiferous aether">luminiferous aether</a>", to transmit its wave motions. Because light can travel through a vacuum, it was assumed that even a vacuum must be filled with aether. Because the <a href="/wiki/Speed_of_light" title="Speed of light">speed of light</a> is so great, and because material bodies pass through the <i>aether</i> without obvious friction or drag, it was assumed to have a highly unusual combination of properties. Designing experiments to test the properties of the aether was a high priority of 19th century physics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Whittaker_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-Whittaker-7">[A 4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>411ff</span></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">Earth</a> orbits around the <a href="/wiki/Sun" title="Sun">Sun</a> at a speed of around 30&#160;km/s (18.64&#160;mi/s), or 108,000&#160;km/h (67,000&#160;mph). The Earth is in motion, so two main possibilities were considered: (1)&#160;The aether is stationary and only partially <a href="/wiki/Drag_(physics)" title="Drag (physics)">dragged</a> by Earth (proposed by <a href="/wiki/Augustin-Jean_Fresnel" title="Augustin-Jean Fresnel">Augustin-Jean Fresnel</a> in 1818), or (2)&#160;the aether is completely dragged by Earth and thus shares its motion at Earth\'s surface (proposed by <a href="/wiki/Sir_George_Stokes,_1st_Baronet" title="Sir George Stokes, 1st Baronet">Sir George Stokes, 1st Baronet</a> in 1844).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jan_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jan-8">[A 5]</a></sup> In addition, <a href="/wiki/James_Clerk_Maxwell" title="James Clerk Maxwell">James Clerk Maxwell</a> (1865) recognized the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electrodynamics" title="Electrodynamics">electromagnetic</a> nature of light and developed what are now called <a href="/wiki/Maxwell%27s_equations" title="Maxwell\'s equations">Maxwell\'s equations</a>, but these equations were still interpreted as describing the motion of waves through an aether, whose state of motion was unknown. Eventually, Fresnel\'s idea of an (almost) stationary aether was preferred because it appeared to be confirmed by the <a href="/wiki/Fizeau_experiment" title="Fizeau experiment">Fizeau experiment</a> (1851) and the <a href="/wiki/Aberration_of_light" title="Aberration of light">aberration of star light</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jan_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-Jan-8">[A 5]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:AetherWind.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="640" decoding="async" height="225" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/AetherWind.svg/300px-AetherWind.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/AetherWind.svg/450px-AetherWind.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/AetherWind.svg/600px-AetherWind.svg.png 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:AetherWind.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Figure 2. A depiction of the concept of the "aether wind"</div></div></div>\n<p>According to the stationary and the partially-dragged aether hypotheses, Earth and the aether are in relative motion, implying that a so-called "aether wind" (Fig.&#160;2) should exist. Although it would be possible, in theory, for the Earth\'s motion to match that of the aether at one moment in time, it was not possible for the Earth to remain at rest with respect to the aether at all times, because of the variation in both the direction and the speed of the motion. At any given point on the Earth\'s surface, the magnitude and direction of the wind would vary with time of day and season. By analyzing the return speed of light in different directions at various different times, it was thought to be possible to measure the motion of the Earth relative to the aether. The expected relative difference in the measured speed of light was quite small, given that the velocity of the Earth in its orbit around the Sun has a magnitude of about one hundredth of one percent of the speed of light.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Whittaker_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-Whittaker-7">[A 4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>417ff</span></sup>\n</p><p>During the mid-19th century, measurements of aether wind effects of first order, i.e. effects proportional to <i>v</i>/<i>c</i> (<i>v</i> being Earth\'s velocity, <i>c</i> the speed of light) were thought to be possible, but no direct measurement of the speed of light was possible with the accuracy required. For instance, the <a href="/wiki/Fizeau%E2%80%93Foucault_apparatus" title="Fizeau&#8211;Foucault apparatus">Fizeau&#8211;Foucault apparatus</a> could measure the speed of light to perhaps 5% accuracy, which was quite inadequate for measuring directly a first-order 0.01% change in the speed of light. A number of physicists therefore attempted to make measurements of indirect first-order effects not of the speed of light itself, but of variations in the speed of light (see <a href="/wiki/Luminiferous_aether#First_order_experiments" title="Luminiferous aether">First order aether-drift experiments</a>). The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hoek_experiment" title="Hoek experiment">Hoek experiment</a>, for example, was intended to detect <a href="/wiki/Interferometry" title="Interferometry">interferometric</a> <a href="/wiki/Fringe_shift" title="Fringe shift">fringe shifts</a> due to speed differences of oppositely propagating light waves through water at rest. The results of such experiments were all negative.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-laub_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-laub-9">[A 6]</a></sup> This could be explained by using <a href="/wiki/Aether_drag_hypothesis#Partial_aether_dragging" title="Aether drag hypothesis">Fresnel\'s dragging coefficient</a>, according to which the aether and thus light are partially dragged by moving matter. Partial aether-dragging would thwart attempts to measure any first order change in the speed of light. As pointed out by Maxwell (1878), only experimental arrangements capable of measuring second order effects would have any hope of detecting aether drift, i.e. effects proportional to <i>v</i><sup>2</sup>/<i>c</i><sup>2</sup>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-maxa_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-maxa-10">[A 7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-maxb_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-maxb-11">[A 8]</a></sup> Existing experimental setups, however, were not sensitive enough to measure effects of that size.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="1881_and_1887_experiments">1881 and 1887 experiments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Michelson%E2%80%93Morley_experiment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: 1881 and 1887 experiments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span id="Michelson_experiment_.281881.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Michelson_experiment_(1881)">Michelson experiment (1881)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Michelson%E2%80%93Morley_experiment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Michelson experiment (1881)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Michelson1881c.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1172" data-file-width="2439" decoding="async" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Michelson1881c.png/300px-Michelson1881c.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Michelson1881c.png/450px-Michelson1881c.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Michelson1881c.png/600px-Michelson1881c.png 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Michelson1881c.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Michelson\'s 1881 interferometer. Although ultimately it proved incapable of distinguishing between differing theories of aether-dragging, its construction provided important lessons for the design of Michelson and Morley\'s 1887 instrument.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[note 1]</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<table class="mbox-small plainlinks sistersitebox" role="presentation" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td class="mbox-image"><img alt="" class="noviewer" data-file-height="430" data-file-width="410" decoding="async" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Wikisource-logo.svg/38px-Wikisource-logo.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Wikisource-logo.svg/57px-Wikisource-logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Wikisource-logo.svg/76px-Wikisource-logo.svg.png 2x" width="38"/></td>\n<td class="mbox-text plainlist"><a href="/wiki/Wikisource" title="Wikisource">Wikisource</a> has original text related to this article:\n<div style="margin-left: 10px;"><b><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/The_Relative_Motion_of_the_Earth_and_the_Luminiferous_Ether" title="wikisource:The Relative Motion of the Earth and the Luminiferous Ether">The Relative Motion of the Earth and the Luminiferous Ether (1881)</a></b></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Michelson had a solution to the problem of how to construct a device sufficiently accurate to detect aether flow. In 1877, while teaching at his alma mater, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Naval_Academy" title="United States Naval Academy">United States Naval Academy</a> in Annapolis, Michelson conducted his first known light speed experiments as a part of a classroom demonstration. In 1881, he left active U.S. Naval service while in Germany concluding his studies. In that year, Michelson used a prototype experimental device to make several more measurements.\n</p><p>The device he designed, later known as a <a href="/wiki/Michelson_interferometer" title="Michelson interferometer">Michelson interferometer</a>, sent <a href="/wiki/Yellow" title="Yellow">yellow</a> light from a <a href="/wiki/Sodium" title="Sodium">sodium</a> flame (for alignment), or <a href="/wiki/White" title="White">white</a> light (for the actual observations), through a <a href="/wiki/Beam_splitter" title="Beam splitter">half-silvered mirror</a> that was used to split it into two beams traveling at right angles to one another. After leaving the splitter, the beams traveled out to the ends of long arms where they were reflected back into the middle by small mirrors. They then recombined on the far side of the splitter in an eyepiece, producing a pattern of constructive and destructive <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interference_(wave_propagation)" title="Interference (wave propagation)">interference</a> whose transverse displacement would depend on the relative time it takes light to transit the longitudinal <i>vs.</i> the transverse arms. If the Earth is traveling through an aether medium, a beam reflecting back and forth parallel to the flow of aether would take longer than a beam reflecting perpendicular to the aether because the time gained from traveling downwind is less than that lost traveling upwind. Michelson expected that the Earth\'s motion would produce a <a href="/wiki/Fringe_shift" title="Fringe shift">fringe shift</a> equal to 0.04 fringes&#8212;that is, of the separation between areas of the same intensity. He did not observe the expected shift; the greatest average deviation that he measured (in the northwest direction) was only 0.018 fringes; most of his measurements were much less. His conclusion was that Fresnel\'s hypothesis of a stationary aether with partial aether dragging would have to be rejected, and thus he confirmed Stokes\' hypothesis of complete aether dragging.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-michel1_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-michel1-13">[4]</a></sup>\n</p><p>However, <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Potier" title="Alfred Potier">Alfred Potier</a> (and later <a href="/wiki/Hendrik_Lorentz" title="Hendrik Lorentz">Hendrik Lorentz</a>) pointed out to Michelson that he had made an error of calculation, and that the expected fringe shift should have been only 0.02 fringes.  Michelson\'s apparatus was subject to experimental errors far too large to say anything conclusive about the aether wind. Definitive measurement of the aether wind would require an experiment with greater accuracy and better controls than the original. Nevertheless, the prototype was successful in demonstrating that the basic method was feasible.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jan_8-2"><a href="#cite_note-Jan-8">[A 5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AIMiller_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-AIMiller-14">[A 9]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Michelson.E2.80.93Morley_experiment_.281887.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Michelson&#8211;Morley_experiment_(1887)">Michelson&#8211;Morley experiment (1887)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Michelson%E2%80%93Morley_experiment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Michelson&#8211;Morley experiment (1887)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="mbox-small plainlinks sistersitebox" role="presentation" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td class="mbox-image"><img alt="" class="noviewer" data-file-height="430" data-file-width="410" decoding="async" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Wikisource-logo.svg/38px-Wikisource-logo.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Wikisource-logo.svg/57px-Wikisource-logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Wikisource-logo.svg/76px-Wikisource-logo.svg.png 2x" width="38"/></td>\n<td class="mbox-text plainlist"><a href="/wiki/Wikisource" title="Wikisource">Wikisource</a> has original text related to this article:\n<div style="margin-left: 10px;"><b><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/On_the_Relative_Motion_of_the_Earth_and_the_Luminiferous_Ether" title="wikisource:On the Relative Motion of the Earth and the Luminiferous Ether">On the Relative Motion of the Earth and the Luminiferous Ether (1887)</a></b></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:On_the_Relative_Motion_of_the_Earth_and_the_Luminiferous_Ether_-_Fig_4.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2684" data-file-width="2160" decoding="async" height="373" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/On_the_Relative_Motion_of_the_Earth_and_the_Luminiferous_Ether_-_Fig_4.png/300px-On_the_Relative_Motion_of_the_Earth_and_the_Luminiferous_Ether_-_Fig_4.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/On_the_Relative_Motion_of_the_Earth_and_the_Luminiferous_Ether_-_Fig_4.png/450px-On_the_Relative_Motion_of_the_Earth_and_the_Luminiferous_Ether_-_Fig_4.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/On_the_Relative_Motion_of_the_Earth_and_the_Luminiferous_Ether_-_Fig_4.png/600px-On_the_Relative_Motion_of_the_Earth_and_the_Luminiferous_Ether_-_Fig_4.png 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:On_the_Relative_Motion_of_the_Earth_and_the_Luminiferous_Ether_-_Fig_4.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Figure 5. This figure illustrates the folded light path used in the Michelson&#8211;Morley interferometer that enabled a path length of 11 m. <i>a</i> is the light source, an oil lamp. <i>b</i> is a beam splitter. <i>c</i> is a compensating plate so that both the reflected and transmitted beams travel through the same amount of glass (important since experiments were run with white light which has an extremely short <a href="/wiki/Coherence_length" title="Coherence length">coherence length</a> requiring precise matching of optical path lengths for fringes to be visible; monochromatic sodium light was used only for initial alignment<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-michel1_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-michel1-13">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[note 2]</a></sup>). <i>d</i>, <i>d\' </i> and <i>e</i> are mirrors. <i>e\' </i> is a fine adjustment mirror. <i>f</i> is a telescope.</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1885, Michelson began a collaboration with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Edward_Morley" title="Edward Morley">Edward Morley</a>, spending considerable time and money to confirm with higher accuracy <a href="/wiki/Fizeau_experiment" title="Fizeau experiment">Fizeau\'s 1851 experiment</a> on Fresnel\'s drag coefficient,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-michel1a_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-michel1a-16">[5]</a></sup> to improve on Michelson\'s 1881 experiment,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-michel2_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-michel2-1">[1]</a></sup> and to establish the wavelength of light as a <a href="/wiki/Length_measurement" title="Length measurement">standard of length</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-michel3_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-michel3-17">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-michel4_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-michel4-18">[7]</a></sup> At this time Michelson was professor of physics at the Case School of Applied Science, and Morley was professor of chemistry at Western Reserve University (WRU), which shared a campus with the Case School on the eastern edge of Cleveland. Michelson suffered a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nervous_breakdown" title="Nervous breakdown">nervous breakdown</a> in September 1885, from which he recovered by October 1885. Morley ascribed this breakdown to the intense work of Michelson during the preparation of the experiments. In 1886, Michelson and Morley successfully confirmed Fresnel\'s drag coefficient &#8211; this result was also considered as a confirmation of the stationary aether concept.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-staley_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-staley-2">[A 1]</a></sup>\n</p><p>This result strengthened their hope of finding the aether wind. Michelson and Morley created an improved version of the Michelson experiment with more than enough accuracy to detect this hypothetical effect. The experiment was performed in several periods of concentrated observations between April and July 1887, in the basement of Adelbert Dormitory of WRU (later renamed Pierce Hall, demolished in 1962).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fickinger_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fickinger-19">[A 10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hamerla_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-hamerla-20">[A 11]</a></sup>\n</p><p>As shown in Fig.&#160;5, the light was repeatedly reflected back and forth along the arms of the interferometer, increasing the path length to 11&#160;m (36&#160;ft). At this length, the drift would be about 0.4 fringes. To make that easily detectable, the apparatus was assembled in a closed room in the basement of the heavy stone dormitory, eliminating most thermal and vibrational effects. Vibrations were further reduced by building the apparatus on top of a large block of sandstone (Fig.&#160;1), about a foot thick and five feet square, which was then floated in a circular trough of mercury. They estimated that effects of about 0.01 fringe would be detectable.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MichelsonCoinAirLumiereBlanche.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2272" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/MichelsonCoinAirLumiereBlanche.JPG/220px-MichelsonCoinAirLumiereBlanche.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/MichelsonCoinAirLumiereBlanche.JPG/330px-MichelsonCoinAirLumiereBlanche.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/MichelsonCoinAirLumiereBlanche.JPG/440px-MichelsonCoinAirLumiereBlanche.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MichelsonCoinAirLumiereBlanche.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Figure 6. Fringe pattern produced with a Michelson interferometer using white light. As configured here, the central fringe is white rather than black.</div></div></div>\n<p>Michelson and Morley and other early experimentalists using interferometric techniques in an attempt to measure the properties of the luminiferous aether, used (partially) monochromatic light only for initially setting up their equipment, always switching to white light for the actual measurements. The reason is that measurements were recorded visually. Purely monochromatic light would result in a uniform fringe pattern. Lacking modern means of <a href="/wiki/Air_conditioning" title="Air conditioning">environmental temperature control</a>, experimentalists struggled with continual fringe drift even when the interferometer was set up in a basement. Because the fringes would occasionally disappear due to vibrations caused by passing horse traffic, distant thunderstorms and the like, an observer could easily "get lost" when the fringes returned to visibility. The advantages of white light, which produced a distinctive colored fringe pattern, far outweighed the difficulties of aligning the apparatus due to its low <a href="/wiki/Coherence_length" title="Coherence length">coherence length</a>. As <a href="/wiki/Dayton_Miller" title="Dayton Miller">Dayton Miller</a> wrote, "White light fringes were chosen for the observations because they consist of a small group of fringes having a central, sharply defined black fringe which forms a permanent zero reference mark for all readings."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Miller1933_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-Miller1933-21">[A 12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[note 3]</a></sup> Use of partially monochromatic light (yellow sodium light) during initial alignment enabled the researchers to locate the position of equal path length, more or less easily, before switching to white light.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[note 4]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The mercury trough allowed the device to turn with close to zero friction, so that once having given the sandstone block a single push it would slowly rotate through the entire range of possible angles to the "aether wind," while measurements were continuously observed by looking through the eyepiece. The hypothesis of aether drift implies that because one of the arms would inevitably turn into the direction of the wind at the same time that another arm was turning perpendicularly to the wind, an effect should be noticeable even over a period of minutes.\n</p><p>The expectation was that the effect would be graphable as a sine wave with two peaks and two troughs per rotation of the device. This result could have been expected because during each full rotation, each arm would be parallel to the wind twice (facing into and away from the wind giving identical readings) and perpendicular to the wind twice. Additionally, due to the Earth\'s rotation, the wind would be expected to show periodic changes in direction and magnitude during the course of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sidereal_day" title="Sidereal day">sidereal day</a>.\n</p><p>Because of the motion of the Earth around the Sun, the measured data were also expected to show annual variations.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Most_famous_.22failed.22_experiment"></span><span class="mw-headline" id=\'Most_famous_"failed"_experiment\'>Most famous "failed" experiment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Michelson%E2%80%93Morley_experiment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title=\'Edit section: Most famous "failed" experiment\'>edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Michelson_Morley_1887_Figure_6.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="396" data-file-width="770" decoding="async" height="154" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/d1/Michelson_Morley_1887_Figure_6.png/300px-Michelson_Morley_1887_Figure_6.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/d1/Michelson_Morley_1887_Figure_6.png/450px-Michelson_Morley_1887_Figure_6.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/d1/Michelson_Morley_1887_Figure_6.png/600px-Michelson_Morley_1887_Figure_6.png 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Michelson_Morley_1887_Figure_6.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Figure 7. Michelson and Morley\'s results. The upper solid line is the curve for their observations at noon, and the lower solid line is that for their evening observations. Note that the theoretical curves and the observed curves are not plotted at the same scale: the dotted curves, in fact, represent only <i>one-eighth of the theoretical displacements.</i></div></div></div>\n<p>After all this thought and preparation, the experiment became what has been called the most famous failed experiment in history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-blum_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-blum-24">[A 13]</a></sup> Instead of providing insight into the properties of the aether, Michelson and Morley\'s article in the <i><a href="/wiki/American_Journal_of_Science" title="American Journal of Science">American Journal of Science</a></i> reported the measurement to be as small as one-fortieth of the expected displacement (Fig.&#160;7), but "since the displacement is proportional to the square of the velocity" they concluded that the measured velocity was "probably less than one-sixth" of the expected velocity of the Earth\'s motion in orbit and "certainly less than one-fourth."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-michel2_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-michel2-1">[1]</a></sup> Although this small "velocity" was measured, it was considered far too small to be used as evidence of speed relative to the aether, and it was understood to be within the range of an experimental error that would allow the speed to actually be zero.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-staley_2-2"><a href="#cite_note-staley-2">[A 1]</a></sup> For instance, Michelson wrote about the "decidedly negative result" in a letter to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lord_Rayleigh" title="Lord Rayleigh">Lord Rayleigh</a> in August 1887:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shankland2_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-shankland2-25">[A 14]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303468">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>The Experiments on the relative motion of the earth and ether have been completed and the result decidedly negative. The expected deviation of the interference fringes from the zero should have been 0.40 of a fringe &#8211; the maximum displacement was 0.02 and the average much less than 0.01 &#8211; and then not in the right place. As displacement is proportional to squares of the relative velocities it follows that if the ether does slip past the relative velocity is less than one sixth of the earth&#8217;s velocity.</p><div class="templatequotecite">&#8212;&#8201;<cite>Albert Abraham Michelson, 1887</cite></div>\n</blockquote>\n<p>From the standpoint of the then current aether models, the experimental results were conflicting. The <a href="/wiki/Fizeau_experiment" title="Fizeau experiment">Fizeau experiment</a> and its 1886 repetition by Michelson and Morley apparently confirmed the stationary aether with partial aether dragging, and refuted complete aether dragging. On the other hand, the much more precise Michelson&#8211;Morley experiment (1887) apparently confirmed complete aether dragging and refuted the stationary aether.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jan_8-3"><a href="#cite_note-Jan-8">[A 5]</a></sup> In addition, the Michelson&#8211;Morley null result was further substantiated by the null results of other second-order experiments of different kind, namely the <a href="/wiki/Trouton%E2%80%93Noble_experiment" title="Trouton&#8211;Noble experiment">Trouton&#8211;Noble experiment</a> (1903) and the <a href="/wiki/Experiments_of_Rayleigh_and_Brace" title="Experiments of Rayleigh and Brace">Experiments of Rayleigh and Brace</a> (1902&#8211;1904). These problems and their solution led to the development of the <a href="/wiki/Lorentz_transformation" title="Lorentz transformation">Lorentz transformation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Special_relativity" title="Special relativity">special relativity</a>.\n</p><p>After the "failed" experiment Michelson and Morley ceased their aether drift measurements and started to use their newly developed technique to establish the wavelength of light as a <a href="/wiki/Length_measurement" title="Length measurement">standard of length</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-michel3_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-michel3-17">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-michel4_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-michel4-18">[7]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Light_path_analysis_and_consequences">Light path analysis and consequences</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Michelson%E2%80%93Morley_experiment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Light path analysis and consequences">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Observer_resting_in_the_aether">Observer resting in the aether</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Michelson%E2%80%93Morley_experiment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Observer resting in the aether">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303569">@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti>.thumbinner{width:100%!important;max-width:none!important}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:none!important;width:100%!important;text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:304px;max-width:304px"><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:302px;max-width:302px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Michelson-morley_calculations.svg"><img alt="Graphical presentation of the expected differential phase shifts in the Michelson&#8211;Morley apparatus" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="595" decoding="async" height="242" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Michelson-morley_calculations.svg/300px-Michelson-morley_calculations.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Michelson-morley_calculations.svg/450px-Michelson-morley_calculations.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Michelson-morley_calculations.svg/600px-Michelson-morley_calculations.svg.png 2x" width="300"/></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:302px;max-width:302px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MichelsonMorleyAnimationDE.gif"><img alt="Animated presentation of the expected differential phase shifts" data-file-height="121" data-file-width="247" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/7c/MichelsonMorleyAnimationDE.gif" width="300"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Figure 4. Expected differential phase shift between light traveling the longitudinal versus the transverse arms of the Michelson&#8211;Morley apparatus</div></div></div></div>\n<p>The beam travel time in the longitudinal direction can be derived as follows:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Feynman_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-Feynman-26">[A 15]</a></sup> Light is sent from the source and propagates with the speed of light <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle c}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>c</mi>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle c}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="c" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/86a67b81c2de995bd608d5b2df50cd8cd7d92455" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.007ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span> in the aether. It passes through the half-silvered mirror at the origin at <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle T=0}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>T</mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mn>0</mn>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle T=0}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="T=0" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/3c6a5b6d0370b358a8d5f3df6d17eeca08d3629b" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:5.897ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span>.  The reflecting mirror is at that moment at distance <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle L}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>L</mi>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle L}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="L" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/103168b86f781fe6e9a4a87b8ea1cebe0ad4ede8" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.583ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> (the length of the interferometer arm) and is moving with velocity <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle v}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>v</mi>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle v}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="v" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/e07b00e7fc0847fbd16391c778d65bc25c452597" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.128ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span>. The beam hits the mirror at time <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle T_{1}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msub>\n<mi>T</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>1</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle T_{1}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="T_{1}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/2f304724948a3ef606c4a92459e22b87a954d993" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.412ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span> and thus travels the distance <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle cT_{1}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>c</mi>\n<msub>\n<mi>T</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>1</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle cT_{1}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="cT_{1}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/e61c11211d9ee438b786df9a5bdf938c80f6eb84" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:3.419ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span>. At this time, the mirror has traveled the distance <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle vT_{1}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>v</mi>\n<msub>\n<mi>T</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>1</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle vT_{1}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="vT_{1}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b1da4807af173184cf944c7507cb8f35b8aa9925" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:3.539ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span>. Thus <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle cT_{1}=L+vT_{1}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>c</mi>\n<msub>\n<mi>T</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>1</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mi>L</mi>\n<mo>+</mo>\n<mi>v</mi>\n<msub>\n<mi>T</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>1</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle cT_{1}=L+vT_{1}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="cT_{1}=L+vT_{1}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/5c3735905d4345aedb48294a66929d3548810d4d" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:14.48ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span> and consequently the travel time <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle T_{1}=L/(c-v)}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msub>\n<mi>T</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>1</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mi>L</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo>/</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mi>c</mi>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mi>v</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle T_{1}=L/(c-v)}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="T_{1}=L/(c-v)" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/5712a817e6d9bf3d25ae07f75710a969e6ffd28c" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:15.04ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span>. The same consideration applies to the backward journey, with the sign of <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle v}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>v</mi>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle v}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="v" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/e07b00e7fc0847fbd16391c778d65bc25c452597" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.128ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span> reversed, resulting in <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle cT_{2}=L-vT_{2}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>c</mi>\n<msub>\n<mi>T</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mi>L</mi>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mi>v</mi>\n<msub>\n<mi>T</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle cT_{2}=L-vT_{2}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="cT_{2}=L-vT_{2}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/bc7024c6cf19fa66bb64281b4225395eae556ca8" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:14.48ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span> and <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle T_{2}=L/(c+v)}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msub>\n<mi>T</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mi>L</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo>/</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mi>c</mi>\n<mo>+</mo>\n<mi>v</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle T_{2}=L/(c+v)}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="T_{2}=L/(c+v)" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/18f64318df1467d3c90e82982667c6ee67609264" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:15.04ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span>. The total travel time <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle T_{l}=T_{1}+T_{2}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msub>\n<mi>T</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>l</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<msub>\n<mi>T</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>1</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>+</mo>\n<msub>\n<mi>T</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle T_{l}=T_{1}+T_{2}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="T_{l}=T_{1}+T_{2}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/226aff4839cc93f53043c87abd977c0357d32e70" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:12.842ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span> is:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle T_{l}={\\frac {L}{c-v}}+{\\frac {L}{c+v}}={\\frac {2L}{c}}{\\frac {1}{1-{\\frac {v^{2}}{c^{2}}}}}\\approx {\\frac {2L}{c}}\\left(1+{\\frac {v^{2}}{c^{2}}}\\right)}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msub>\n<mi>T</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>l</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mi>L</mi>\n<mrow>\n<mi>c</mi>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mi>v</mi>\n</mrow>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<mo>+</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mi>L</mi>\n<mrow>\n<mi>c</mi>\n<mo>+</mo>\n<mi>v</mi>\n</mrow>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mrow>\n<mn>2</mn>\n<mi>L</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mi>c</mi>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mn>1</mn>\n<mrow>\n<mn>1</mn>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<msup>\n<mi>v</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<msup>\n<mi>c</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<mo>&#8776;<!-- &#8776; --></mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mrow>\n<mn>2</mn>\n<mi>L</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mi>c</mi>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<mrow>\n<mo>(</mo>\n<mrow>\n<mn>1</mn>\n<mo>+</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<msup>\n<mi>v</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<msup>\n<mi>c</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n<mo>)</mo>\n</mrow>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle T_{l}={\\frac {L}{c-v}}+{\\frac {L}{c+v}}={\\frac {2L}{c}}{\\frac {1}{1-{\\frac {v^{2}}{c^{2}}}}}\\approx {\\frac {2L}{c}}\\left(1+{\\frac {v^{2}}{c^{2}}}\\right)}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle T_{l}={\\frac {L}{c-v}}+{\\frac {L}{c+v}}={\\frac {2L}{c}}{\\frac {1}{1-{\\frac {v^{2}}{c^{2}}}}}\\approx {\\frac {2L}{c}}\\left(1+{\\frac {v^{2}}{c^{2}}}\\right)}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/7dfee42a2db1aa26b392aff4da4bc18be61565b8" style="vertical-align: -4.005ex; width:51.134ex; height:7.843ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>Michelson obtained this expression correctly in 1881, however, in transverse direction he obtained the incorrect expression\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle T_{t}={\\frac {2L}{c}},}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msub>\n<mi>T</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>t</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mrow>\n<mn>2</mn>\n<mi>L</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mi>c</mi>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<mo>,</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle T_{t}={\\frac {2L}{c}},}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle T_{t}={\\frac {2L}{c}},}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/5035925a3c7158c310a243164d9a10f2b1e91eca" style="vertical-align: -1.838ex; width:9.51ex; height:5.176ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>because he overlooked that the aether wind also affects the transverse beam travel time. This was corrected by <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Potier" title="Alfred Potier">Alfred Potier</a> (1882) and Lorentz (1886). The derivation in the transverse direction can be given as follows (analogous to the derivation of <a href="/wiki/Time_dilation" title="Time dilation">time dilation</a> using a <a href="/wiki/Time_dilation#Simple_inference_of_time_dilation_due_to_relative_velocity" title="Time dilation">light clock</a>): The beam is propagating at the speed of light <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle c}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>c</mi>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle c}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="c" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/86a67b81c2de995bd608d5b2df50cd8cd7d92455" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.007ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span> and hits the mirror at time <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle T_{3}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msub>\n<mi>T</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>3</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle T_{3}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="T_{3}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ac0936b6ba76bf0d900bb7315c99f64c5376f5ed" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.412ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span>, traveling the distance <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle cT_{3}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>c</mi>\n<msub>\n<mi>T</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>3</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle cT_{3}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="cT_{3}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/1dfa22eeedc03d44776c49627bc487b4ce909825" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:3.419ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span>. At the same time, the mirror has traveled the distance <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle vT_{3}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>v</mi>\n<msub>\n<mi>T</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>3</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle vT_{3}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="vT_{3}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f2f548bf290f59cb1a4617fd3fff56fa9d314f43" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:3.539ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span> in the <i>x</i> direction. So in order to hit the mirror, the travel path of the beam is <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle L}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>L</mi>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle L}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="L" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/103168b86f781fe6e9a4a87b8ea1cebe0ad4ede8" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.583ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> in the <i>y</i> direction (assuming equal-length arms) and <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle vT_{3}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>v</mi>\n<msub>\n<mi>T</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>3</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle vT_{3}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="vT_{3}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f2f548bf290f59cb1a4617fd3fff56fa9d314f43" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:3.539ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span> in the <i>x</i> direction. This inclined travel path follows from the transformation from the interferometer rest frame to the aether rest frame. Therefore, the <a href="/wiki/Pythagorean_theorem" title="Pythagorean theorem">Pythagorean theorem</a> gives the actual beam travel distance of <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\scriptstyle {\\sqrt {L^{2}+\\left(vT_{3}\\right)^{2}}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mstyle displaystyle="false" scriptlevel="1">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<msqrt>\n<msup>\n<mi>L</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mo>+</mo>\n<msup>\n<mrow>\n<mo>(</mo>\n<mrow>\n<mi>v</mi>\n<msub>\n<mi>T</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>3</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n</mrow>\n<mo>)</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n</msqrt>\n</mrow>\n</mstyle>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\scriptstyle {\\sqrt {L^{2}+\\left(vT_{3}\\right)^{2}}}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="\\scriptstyle {\\sqrt {L^{2}+\\left(vT_{3}\\right)^{2}}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/19e8dd63812c4718b1f75a1a2b29d37fc1d4a10e" style="vertical-align: -1.171ex; width:9.572ex; height:3.509ex;"/></span>. Thus <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\scriptstyle cT_{3}={\\sqrt {L^{2}+\\left(vT_{3}\\right)^{2}}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mstyle displaystyle="false" scriptlevel="1">\n<mi>c</mi>\n<msub>\n<mi>T</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>3</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<msqrt>\n<msup>\n<mi>L</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mo>+</mo>\n<msup>\n<mrow>\n<mo>(</mo>\n<mrow>\n<mi>v</mi>\n<msub>\n<mi>T</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>3</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n</mrow>\n<mo>)</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n</msqrt>\n</mrow>\n</mstyle>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\scriptstyle cT_{3}={\\sqrt {L^{2}+\\left(vT_{3}\\right)^{2}}}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="\\scriptstyle cT_{3}={\\sqrt {L^{2}+\\left(vT_{3}\\right)^{2}}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/3834e3660c37fb83d95b18251af8fc3405786218" style="vertical-align: -1.171ex; width:13.354ex; height:3.509ex;"/></span> and consequently the travel time <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\scriptstyle T_{3}=L/{\\sqrt {c^{2}-v^{2}}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mstyle displaystyle="false" scriptlevel="1">\n<msub>\n<mi>T</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>3</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mi>L</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo>/</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<msqrt>\n<msup>\n<mi>c</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<msup>\n<mi>v</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n</msqrt>\n</mrow>\n</mstyle>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\scriptstyle T_{3}=L/{\\sqrt {c^{2}-v^{2}}}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="\\scriptstyle T_{3}=L/{\\sqrt {c^{2}-v^{2}}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ebc583dfdedc339f876f520a0baab06e77319ff2" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:11.105ex; height:2.676ex;"/></span>, which is the same for the backward journey. The total travel time <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle T_{t}=2T_{3}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msub>\n<mi>T</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>t</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mn>2</mn>\n<msub>\n<mi>T</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>3</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle T_{t}=2T_{3}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="T_{t}=2T_{3}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/95c141ece431d7eba1d12023849c3a1ec4c0fb05" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:8.856ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span> is:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle T_{t}={\\frac {2L}{\\sqrt {c^{2}-v^{2}}}}={\\frac {2L}{c}}{\\frac {1}{\\sqrt {1-{\\frac {v^{2}}{c^{2}}}}}}\\approx {\\frac {2L}{c}}\\left(1+{\\frac {v^{2}}{2c^{2}}}\\right)}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msub>\n<mi>T</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>t</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mrow>\n<mn>2</mn>\n<mi>L</mi>\n</mrow>\n<msqrt>\n<msup>\n<mi>c</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722;
