Data between 2007&#8211;2008 was analyzed.</td>\n<td rowspan="2"><center><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\lesssim 10^{-17}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mo>&#8818;<!-- &#8818; --></mo>\n<msup>\n<mn>10</mn>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mn>17</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\lesssim 10^{-17}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="\\lesssim 10^{-17}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/14ff10768a51cdcd50182b88178d4ae2906b05d0" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:7.933ex; height:3.176ex;"/></span></center>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="white-space:nowrap;">Herrmann <i>et al.</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Herrmann2_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-Herrmann2-5">[3]</a></sup></td>\n<td>2009</td>\n<td>Similar to Herrmann <i>et al.</i> (2005). The frequencies of a pair of rotating, orthogonal optical <a href="/wiki/Fabry%E2%80%93P%C3%A9rot_interferometer" title="Fabry&#8211;P&#233;rot interferometer">Fabry&#8211;P&#233;rot resonators</a> are compared. The frequencies of two <a href="/wiki/Nd:YAG_laser" title="Nd:YAG laser">Nd:YAG lasers</a> are stabilized to resonances of these resonators.\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_tests_of_Lorentz_invariance">Other tests of Lorentz invariance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Michelson%E2%80%93Morley_experiment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Other tests of Lorentz invariance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Modern_searches_for_Lorentz_violation" title="Modern searches for Lorentz violation">Modern searches for Lorentz violation</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:227px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lithium-7-NMR_spectrum_of_LiCl_(1M)_in_D2O.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="354" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Lithium-7-NMR_spectrum_of_LiCl_%281M%29_in_D2O.gif/225px-Lithium-7-NMR_spectrum_of_LiCl_%281M%29_in_D2O.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Lithium-7-NMR_spectrum_of_LiCl_%281M%29_in_D2O.gif/338px-Lithium-7-NMR_spectrum_of_LiCl_%281M%29_in_D2O.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Lithium-7-NMR_spectrum_of_LiCl_%281M%29_in_D2O.gif/450px-Lithium-7-NMR_spectrum_of_LiCl_%281M%29_in_D2O.gif 2x" width="225"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lithium-7-NMR_spectrum_of_LiCl_(1M)_in_D2O.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Figure 10. <sup>7</sup>Li-NMR spectrum of LiCl (1M) in D<sub>2</sub>O. The sharp, unsplit NMR line of this isotope of lithium is evidence for the isotropy of mass and space.</div></div></div>\n<p>Examples of other experiments not based on the Michelson&#8211;Morley principle, i.e. non-optical isotropy tests achieving an even higher level of precision, are <a href="/wiki/Hughes%E2%80%93Drever_experiment" title="Hughes&#8211;Drever experiment">Clock comparison or Hughes&#8211;Drever experiments</a>. In Drever\'s 1961 experiment, <sup>7</sup>Li nuclei in the ground state, which has total angular momentum <i>J</i>=3/2, were split into four equally spaced levels by a magnetic field. Each transition between a pair of adjacent levels should emit a photon of equal frequency, resulting in a single, sharp spectral line. However, since the nuclear wave functions for different <i>M<sub>J</sub></i> have different orientations in space relative to the magnetic field, any orientation dependence, whether from an aether wind or from a dependence on the large-scale distribution of mass in space (see <a href="/wiki/Mach%27s_principle" title="Mach\'s principle">Mach\'s principle</a>), would perturb the energy spacings between the four levels, resulting in an anomalous broadening or splitting of the line. No such broadening was observed. Modern repeats of this kind of experiment have provided some of the most accurate confirmations of the principle of <a href="/wiki/Lorentz_covariance" title="Lorentz covariance">Lorentz invariance</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-haugan_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-haugan-80">[A 36]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Michelson%E2%80%93Morley_experiment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Michelson%E2%80%93Morley_Award" title="Michelson&#8211;Morley Award">Michelson&#8211;Morley Award</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Moving_magnet_and_conductor_problem" title="Moving magnet and conductor problem">Moving magnet and conductor problem</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/The_Light_(Glass)" title="The Light (Glass)"><i>The Light</i> (Glass)</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/LIGO" title="LIGO">LIGO</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Michelson%E2%80%93Morley_experiment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Michelson%E2%80%93Morley_experiment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 60em; -webkit-column-width: 60em; column-width: 60em; list-style-type: decimal;">\n<ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-12"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-12">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Among other lessons was the need to control for vibration. Michelson (1881) wrote: "...&#160;owing to the extreme sensitiveness of the instrument to vibrations, the work could not be carried on during the day. Next, the experiment was tried at night. When the mirrors were placed half-way on the arms the fringes were visible, but their position could not be measured till after twelve o\'clock, and then only at intervals. When the mirrors were moved out to the ends of the arms, the fringes were only occasionally visible. It thus appeared that the experiments could not be performed in Berlin, and the apparatus was accordingly removed to the Astrophysicalisches Observatorium in Potsdam&#160;... Here, the fringes under ordinary circumstances were sufficiently quiet to measure, but so extraordinarily sensitive was the instrument that the stamping of the pavement, about 100 meters from the observatory, made the fringes disappear entirely!"</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-15"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-15">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Michelson (1881) wrote: "...&#160;a sodium flame placed at <i>a</i> produced at once the interference bands. These could then be altered in width, position, or direction, by a slight movement of the plate <i>b</i>, and when they were of convenient width and of maximum sharpness, the sodium flame was removed and the lamp again substituted. The screw <i>m</i> was then slowly turned till the bands reappeared. They were then of course colored, except the central band, which was nearly black."</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-22"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-22">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">If one uses a half-silvered mirror as the beam splitter, the reflected beam will undergo a different number of front-surface reflections than the transmitted beam. At each front-surface reflection, the light will undergo a phase inversion. Because the two beams undergo a different number of phase inversions, when the path lengths of the two beams match or differ by an integral number of wavelengths (e.g. 0, 1, 2&#160;...), there will be destructive interference and a weak signal at the detector. If the path lengths of the beams differ by a half-integral number of wavelengths (e.g., 0.5, 1.5, 2.5&#160;...), constructive interference will yield a strong signal. The results are opposite if a cube beam-splitter is used, because a cube beam-splitter makes no distinction between a front- and rear-surface reflection.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-23"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-23">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Sodium light produces a fringe pattern that displays cycles of fuzziness and sharpness that repeat every several hundred fringes over a distance of approximately a millimeter. This pattern is due to the yellow sodium D line being actually a doublet, the individual lines of which have a limited <a href="/wiki/Coherence_length" title="Coherence length">coherence length</a>. After aligning the interferometer to display the centermost portion of the sharpest set of fringes, the researcher would switch to white light.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-Thirring-49"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Thirring_49-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Thirring (1926) as well as Lorentz pointed out that Miller\'s results failed even the most basic criteria required to believe in their celestial origin, namely that the azimuth of supposed drift should exhibit daily variations consistent with the source rotating about the celestial pole. Instead, while Miller\'s observations showed daily variations, their oscillations in one set of experiments might center, say, around a northwest&#8211;southeast line.</span>\n</li>\n</ol></div>\n<p><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[40]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Experiments">Experiments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Michelson%E2%80%93Morley_experiment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Experiments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">\n<ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-michel2-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-michel2_1-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-michel2_1-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-michel2_1-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-michel2_1-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-michel2_1-4"><sup><i><b>e</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation journal">Michelson, Albert A.; Morley, Edward W. (1886). <span class="cs1-ws-icon" title="s:Influence of Motion of the Medium on the Velocity of Light"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Influence_of_Motion_of_the_Medium_on_the_Velocity_of_Light">"Influence of Motion of the Medium on the Velocity of Light"&#160;</a></span>. <i>Am.
